U.S. Pending Home Sales Rebounded in September; Tight inventory and low mortgage rates extend choppy trend
By Ben Leubsdorf
504 words
27 October 2016
11:19
The Wall Street Journal Online
WSJO
English
Copyright 2016 Dow Jones & Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved.

WASHINGTON—A gauge of coming U.S. home sales moved higher in September after falling the prior month, extending a recent choppy trend amid tight inventory and low mortgage rates.

The National Association of Realtors said Thursday that its pending home sales index[http://www.realtor.org/topics/pending-home-sales], which tracks contract signings for previously owned homes, rose 1.5% from August to a seasonally adjusted 110.0. Sales typically close within a month or two of signing.

Economists surveyed by The Wall Street Journal had expected a more modest rise of 1.0%.

"This latest increase suggests that existing home sales…will increase in the coming months," J.P. Morgan Chase economist Daniel Silver said in a note to clients. "But even with this latest gain in pending home sales, the trend in the data has softened lately."

The index has fluctuated in recent months after spiking in April[http://www.wsj.com.proxy.library.brocku.ca/articles/pending-home-sales-climbed-to-highest-level-in-10-years-1464271244]. It was 111.2 in July and fell in August[http://www.wsj.com.proxy.library.brocku.ca/articles/pending-home-sales-fall-2-4-in-august-1475157822] to 108.4, reduced slightly from an earlier estimate of 108.5, before partly rebounding in September. Compared with a year earlier, pending home sales in September were up 2.4%.

"Although depressed inventory levels are keeping home prices elevated in most of the country, steady job gains and growing evidence that wages are finally starting to tick up are encouraging more households to consider buying a home," said Lawrence Yun, the trade group's chief economist.

The near-term outlook for sales remains uncertain.

Thursday's report "suggests little change in actual existing home sales in October," MFR Inc. chief U.S. economist Joshua Shapiro said in a note to clients.

But Pantheon Macroeconomics chief economist Ian Shepherdson said in a note to clients that "existing home sales overshot relative to pending sales in September, so today's data are consistent with a dip in October existing home sales."

News Corp, owner of The Wall Street Journal, also operates Realtor.com under license from the National Association of Realtors.

Purchases of existing homes, which account for roughly 90% of U.S. homebuying activity, peaked in June at an annualized sales rate of 5.57 million, the strongest monthly reading since February 2007. Sales weakened in July and August but rebounded in September[http://www.wsj.com.proxy.library.brocku.ca/articles/u-s-existing-home-sales-rebounded-in-september-1476972399], rising 3.2% from the prior month to a seasonally adjusted annual rate of 5.47 million, the National Association of Realtors said last week.

Borrowing costs remain low for prospective home buyers. The average interest rate on a 30-year fixed-rate mortgage in September was 3.46%, down from 3.89% a year earlier, according to Freddie Mac[http://www.freddiemac.com/pmms/pmms30.htm].

But tight inventory has put upward pressure on home prices, hindering some would-be buyers.

Federal Reserve officials in September judged that "the sluggishness in the housing sector appeared to have continued into the third quarter," according to minutes of their Sept. 20-21 policy meeting[http://www.federalreserve.gov.proxy.library.brocku.ca/monetarypolicy/fomcminutes20160921.htm].

Husky Energy Swings to Profit on Gains; Sale of energy assets helped, as production and average prices trailed year-earlier levels
By Judy McKinnon

27 October 2016
08:07
The Wall Street Journal Online
WSJO
English
Copyright 2016 Dow Jones & Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved.

Husky Energy Inc. posted a third-quarter profit on Thursday, largely due to hefty gains on the sale of energy assets[http://www.wsj.com.proxy.library.brocku.ca/articles/canadas-husky-energy-posts-another-quarterly-loss-1461629202], while production and average prices trailed year-earlier levels.

The Calgary, Alberta-based oil and gas producer has had a string of quarterly losses until now, hurt by a continuing slump in oil prices[http://www.wsj.com.proxy.library.brocku.ca/articles/falling-crude-prices-upend-canadas-oil-sands-projects-1437609134] that has curbed profits in the oil patch.

Husky had a net profit of 1.39 billion Canadian dollars ($1.04 billion), or C$1.37 a share, in its latest quarter ended Sept. 30. That compares with a small loss in the second quarter[http://www.wsj.com.proxy.library.brocku.ca/articles/husky-energy-swings-to-a-loss-on-lower-output-1469190601] and a loss of C$4.1 billion a year earlier.

Adjusted to exclude nearly C$1.5 billion of gains on the sale of assets in Western Canada, however, Husky said it lost C$100 million, compared with a loss of C$101 million on the same basis a year earlier.

The company said that, despite the volatility in oil prices over the past two years, its balance sheet is strong and net debt is in line with its target. Husky cut its net debt to C$4.1 billion at the end of the latest quarter from C$6.8 billion a year earlier, helped in part by the C$1.7 billion sale of a group of Canadian midstream assets in April to two Hong Kong-based firms.

Husky, an affiliate of Hong Kong conglomerate CK Hutchison Holdings, said cash flow fell to C$484 million from C$674 million a year earlier. Overall production dipped to 301,000 barrels of oil equivalent a day from 333,000 barrels a day a year earlier, while average realized prices were down about 16% year-over-year.

Husky's results come just hours after the company announced a surprise management shuffle that will see its chief operating officer replace its chief executive. Asim Ghosh, chief executive since June 2010, will step down in December and be succeeded by Chief Operating Officer Rob Peabody.

27 October 2016
The Wall Street Journal

English

EDUCATION

College Tuition Rises

At Modest Pace

Tuition increases at U.S. colleges rose relatively slowly during the 2016-17 academic year after rapid gains during and after the 2007-09 recession, but stagnant wages, low inflation and a slight pullback in grants continue to amplify those modest jumps and fuel concern about college affordability.

Published tuition for the 2016-17 academic year rose about 2.4% for in-state students at four-year public schools -- down from 2.9% last year, according to a report released Wednesday from the College Board, a New York nonprofit that tracks university costs.

In-state students attending public four-year institutions now pay $20,090 on average for tuition, fees and room and board, up from $19,570 in 2015-16. Private-school costs rose $1,500from the previous academic yearto $45,370.

-- Douglas Belkin

ECONOMY

Sales of New Homes

Rose 3.1% Last Month

Sales of newly built homes rose in September after an August tumble, a sign that modest momentum continues in the housing market.

Purchases of new single-family homes increased 3.1% in September from the prior month to a seasonally adjusted annual rate of 593,000, the Commerce Department said Wednesday.

Through the first nine months of the year, sales were up 13% compared with the same period in 2015. That measure is consistent with other gauges of the housing market showing improvement through most of this year.

-- Eric Morath

---

CALIFORNIA

Death Penalty to Be

Sought in Killings

Prosecutors will seek the death penalty for the man accused of murdering two police officers in Palm Springs earlier this month.

After meeting with the officers' families Wednesday, Riverside County District Attorney Mike Hestrin announced that he would seek the death penalty for alleged killer John Hernandez Felix.

Mr. Felix, 26 years old, is accused of gunning down Palm Springs Officers Jose Gilbert Vega and Lesley Zerebny on Oct. 8 after they responded to a domestic disturbance call at a home. A third officer was injured in the shooting.

Michael Rowlands, an attorney for Mr. Felix, declined to comment. Mr. Felix has pleaded not guilty.

-- Zusha Elinson
